I use NiMH batteries which last over 1 week of normal shaving (about 2-3 minutes per day). The main downside to this shaver is the lack of a beard trimmer which I've gotten used to with most of the other travel razors I've used. You can rinse off the head under flowing tap water to clean it, which you should do immediately after each use. All in all a fairly decent razor for the price. Best of all the batteries will never die on you away from an electrical outlet. All you have to do is buy some alkaline AA's if you run out of rechargeables. For this price you can buy a complete razor for less than the price of a single replacement foil.

  85. A couple clarifications, because these reviews refer to several different model years. As of January 2012, this razor does *not* have a pop-up trimmer. It does not have a full case, but comes with a plastic guard that snaps over the foils.<br /><br />Those notes aside, this is a really nifty little razor. I'd expected it to be a little smaller, as it's half the size of my normal Braun, but that's fine. The shape fits nicely in my hand and is easy to hold. The power switch has a spring detente so it doesn't turn itself on in your bag. The battery compartment door has a neat screw-lock mechanism (finger operated) that properly seals the door; I believe them when they say it's waterproof. The razor is a little noisy in use, but that's to be expected. It does a fine job actually shaving. I have a lot of sideways-growing hair follicles, and foil razors do the best job. This works at least as well as my old Braun, and maybe better, as it's nice and new. Shaving takes about the same amount of time as with my full-size, and leaves a nice smooth finish, with no irritation. I miss the pop-up trimmer a little, but it's not a concern while travelling. I'd like a full-body case, but that would add size, and the plastic guard for the foil seems sturdy and snaps on firmly. All in all, a very nice travel razor.

  117. Panasonic has a pretty extensive line of cordless electric shavers, and choosing one can be a little challenging. I went with the black ES3831K Pro-Curve Wet/Dry Travel Shaver because of its small size and low price, and so far have not been disappointed with its performance. Powered by two AA batteries, the motor seems quite powerful, and hums along quietly without being annoying. It is shaped to fit nicely in the hand, and feels quite solid and hefty, not cheap or flimsy. It is designed to be used wet or dry, but I intend to keep exposure to water to a minimum. I don't have a heavy beard, and this shaver gives a nice close painfree shave, without any nicks or skin irritation.<br /><br />The on/off switch is larger than it needs to be, and sometimes sticks, but that's about all there is to complain about. Pushing a button releases the cover, and exposes the blades, which are easy to clean. A tiny cleaning brush comes with the shaver, but you may want to use something more substantial, like an old toothbrush. If you use rechargeable batteries, battery life isn't an issue. The shaver works fine, even with lower powered 1.2 volt, 1600 mAh NiMH batteries. Although the description says it comes with a case, mine did not.<br /><br />The blade and metal screen (foil) over the blades are made of stainless steel. For electric shavers, the screen is typically what breaks first, and replacement costs are often substantial. It is probably a good idea to keep the clear plastic cover that fits over the screen on, whenever the shaver is not in use. Since it does not use a rechargeable battery, depending on costs, it may be more economical to get a new shaver, versus buying a replacement blade or foil.<br /><br />The Pro-Curve works well and is so inexpensive, that I may get another to carry around with me, or leave in the car for a quick touch up. It would also make a great gift.

Personally, I prefer rechargeable AA batteries, and it's nice to be able to keep some charging to instantly swap them out when I feel this shaver is running a little slow. This is way better than the drawback of shavers containing built-in batteries. You can't remove them when they start declining in performance, and you have to wait for the recharge cycle to do its thing.<br /><br />You can't beat the price, either. It's cheaper than buying replacement blades/screens for most shavers, including this one. Yes, you heard me right--you are better off buying a new one of these than the replacement parts for it. Start stocking up on these now. If the company making these goes out of business and this unit stops being produced, the replacement parts may go on sale. At that point, if you purchased a bunch of these units over the years, you could pick up a whole bunch of spare screens/blades on sale and never buy another shaver. That's my theory.

  331. For many years, I’ve been using one of those well-known electric razors with the three floating heads. I’ve always been satisfied with the clean shave it gives me, but I’ve also been annoyed by the amount of time it takes to get it. Seems like it’s necessary to go over the same area again and again to finally get everything shaved off clean. For me, shaving has always been a necessary nuisance and I had hoped that changing over to an electric razor would lessen the daily drudgery. It didn’t.<br /><br />Then, on a whim, I bought one of these little Panasonic battery-operated razors. I knew that the cutting technology was different from what I was using and I wanted to see how well it performed. After all, fourteen bucks wasn’t going to break me if it didn’t work. I placed my order and three days later, my new toy arrived. Time to give it a try.<br /><br />Wow! Color me impressed! Very, very favorably impressed. Just one pass over any area of skin with two days of beard growth resulted in a dead-smooth shave. No scrubbing necessary. No need to go over the same area again and again. I got a totally clean shave in about one-third the time it took with my old electric razor. I’m totally delighted with the performance of this Panasonic razor. I can’t find anything to criticize about it. It has a pleasing appearance, it’s well balanced, it’s easy to maneuver around the little nooks and crannies of your face and it just plain feels good in your hand. This little razor almost makes shaving fun. Almost, I said.<br /><br />There is one caveat though: While this thing works great for removing one or two days of beard growth, it doesn’t work very well at removing longer growth. That’s because in order to be cut off, hairs must first be able to enter the tiny holes in the shaving head’s thin metal foil so that they are exposed to the cutter blades on the other side of the foil. Short hairs do this easily. But longer ones get pushed over on their side and the foil simply slides over them. They don’t enter the holes, so they don’t get severed by the cutters. With enough scrubbing and scouring, you can eventually get these longer hairs cut off too, but by then your face may be pretty raw and you’ll probably decide that all the extra work and effort just isn’t worth it. For me, that’s when I break out my old blade razor. The simplest solution, of course, is to not go more than two or three days without shaving. Keeps the wife happy too.<br /><br />So yes, I would most definitely recommend this product to a family member, or friend, or anyone else who wants to lessen the drudgery of their daily shave. Well done, Panasonic!

For that matter it runs stronger and better than my standard, home edition Braun. Let me put it up front: I'm a big Braun fan, they have served me well for years, but this inexpensive Panasonic travel sharpener is good enough, for me, for home use. It also has a great shape, great industrial design, did they hire Braun's designer or give someone with a new way of looking at things free reign to innovate? 'cause this is amazingly good looking and strong performing, shocking at $15 (batteries not included!).<br /><br />Pluses and minuses:<br /><br />+ Produces high RPM from fresh AA's. (I will add an update when I have used this for a couple of weeks, how long it takes to decline and what it's like towards the end.) Since this is a pretty good shaver, I may try Lithium AA's which are actually cheaper than the more traditional alkalines, if you look at total power available vs. cost (although the initial cost is quite higher). Note that Lithiums have a very steep power drop off - which is good - they deliver their full power and hence rpm right up until the end, then drop off quickly. So you won't be faced with the quandary of trying to keep going on alkalines that still have enough power for a shave but not enough power for good performance. [[ASIN:B0044P3J2I Energizer Ultimate Lithium AA 12 Battery Super Pack]] Lithiums last a lot longer - up to 9x as long in the Ultimate edition - and weigh much less than alkalines which is also good if you are going on an extended trip or hike.<br /><br />+ Shaves closer than either of my Brauns.<br />- I haven't had shaver burn from an electric in years - since my skin is conditioned to them. But with this one shaving closer, I have some shaver burn spots now.<br /><br />+ Shaves close enough that I could, in a pinch, get away without my normal \\"touch up\\" shave with a blade in the shower.<br />- It's still not as close as a good blade with careful work, but it will certainly pass for dinner or a date.<br /><br />- No edge trimmer. I don't use this much, preferring to use a blade, but you need to know this.<br />- Due to the lack of edge trimmer and almost all electric shavers' inability to cut down the occasional stray (longer) hair, you will need to carry a disposable blade for touch ups.<br /><br />+ Has a tiny button in the on-off slider which keeps the slider locked until you depress it. This is good for travel.<br /><br />+ It is water proof so it's harder to mess up. I don't do wet (shower) shaving so I don't know how well that works - I don't like leaving the head damp. I will keep it in mind for my periodic deep cleaning though - it's nice to know I can wash this is a bowl of soapy water and don't have to use those old-fashioned shaver cleaner liquids.<br /><br />+ Nicely designed, nice fitting clip-on clear plastic shaver head cover.<br />- The cover doesn't have vent slots for drying out, an issue if you wet-shave with this.<br /><br />- + Bigger and heavier than other travel shavers - but still MUCH lighter than a home shaver. Gram shavers need an Eltron and you can even save a couple of ounces and some space with a Braun.<br /><br />- + The tiny utility brush doesn't fit into a slot on the shaver, and my prediction is you will lose it quickly. But hey there's always your toothbrush, right?<br /><br />I'll update here as necessary. It's good enough for daily shaving so I won't have to wait for a trip get a significant number of shaves on it.<br /><br />Notes: caucasian beard, lightly bearded but what I have is stubbly. Usually light to medium electric shave followed by a touch-up in the shower with a BIC single edge disposable razor.<br /><br />I wasn't in the market for a travel shaver, but a website reviewed the top3 - Braun, Eltron and this one ([[ASIN:B002TQ4AO0 Braun Mobile Shaver - M90 1 Count]], [[ASIN:B001IDZMGK Eltron #el-3040 Compact Travel Shaver]]} - and commenters liked the Panasonic so I thought I'd give it a try. I'm glad that I did.<br /><br />Update: 17 days on my first set of AA batteries (Rayovac alkalines). August 30-Sept 15).<br />Update: 17 days on my second set of AA batteries (Rayovac's again). Sept 16-October 2. Surprisingly consistent. No more razor burn! Either the blade burnished in, or my skin toughened up.<br />Update: Oct 3 to Oct 13 on third set of AA batteries (Rayovac's again). Fewer days of life - did these batteries come out of another device, they were rattling loose in the drawer. Chalk this one up as an anomaly given the consistent performance of the first 2 sets.<br />Update: October 14 until January 19 (!!! yes true) on one set of Energizer Advanced Lithium AA's. So apparently lithium batteries do last a lot longer. That was about 97 days. So the $2 a piece cost of the battery (vs. .50 cents for alkalines) is more than recovered. The \\"death spiral\\" of lithiums is even more drawn out than alkalines however - it was running slow (but enough to shave) for about 10 days before they gave up the ghost.3 - Braun, Eltron and this one ([[ASIN:B002TQ4AO0 Braun Mobile Shaver - M90 1 Count]], [[ASIN:B001IDZMGK Eltron #el-3040 Compact Travel Shaver]]} - and commenters liked the Panasonic so I thought I'd give it a try.   654. ~~~~~~~~~<br />\\"Do not use rechargeable batteries. Doing so may result in the leakage of the battery and the malfunction.\\"<br />~~~~~~~~~<br />This is the exact wording of a segment from the manual of the Panasonic ES 3831 K (not quite correct English and not-quite-great-recommendation of disposable batteries).<br /><br />The back of the box also specifically mentions alkaline no less than 3 times (!).<br /><br />A voice inside my head:<br />\\"Hold on a second, is this the year 2013 or 1973?\\"<br />Why are people still using disposables?<br /><br />I'm at a loss when Panasonic suggest leakage with rechargeables when alkaline batteries are known for their leakage (and I have experienced it with alkalines but never with my rechargeables so far, though I'm not suggesting it's impossible either). Assuming rechargeables leak, at the very least both battery technologies should be equally recommendable, right?<br /><br />All companies like to talk 'green' but in reality (such as with Panasonic's insistence of disposable batteries here) they are doing precious little. What I don't understand is that Panasonic make rechargeable batteries as well as disposables, so I'm assuming there is some technical reason other than pure profit at play here. If so, I'm dying to know what that is.<br /><br />Sanyo was bought by Panasonic a few years back and now Panasonic own their excellent Eneloop battery technology, which makes it all the more bizarre to see alkaline be suggested so strongly in favour of rechargeables in the ES3831K shaver manual.<br /><br />PANASONIC SPARES (and waste stories)<br />Let's take into account the cost of this device. Then let's observe the little slip of paper that comes with this shaver with the heading \\"Replacement Parts and Accessories Wet/Dry Battery Shaver ES3831\\"<br /><br />It goes on to list replacement part prices in US dollars. The outer foil and inner blade are basically 5 cents short of ten dollars each. Panasonic recommend replacing the outer foilonce a year and the blade every 2 years, according to the manual. I'll let you decide whether you think it's worth getting replacements or buying another unit. Yet another device designed to be disposed of and bought again.<br /><br />This is the hideously wasteful world we live in and mormally I try to avoid products priced like this (consumables more than the device).<br /><br />You don't have to be a genius to figure out the consequences this colossal waste and re-consumption has on the environment, especially when multiplied by hundreds of thousands of people around the world who would buy such a device. Panasonic do a similar thing with their higher-priced shavers with integrated rechargeable batteries: in their manuals they explicitly suggest the user does not replace the battery themselves, but instead insists we disassemble and dispose of it properly (I can see that happening...). If wanting replacement by chance, we should let Panasonic handle it and never attempt to replace the battery ourselves. Cost...who knows. Probably a nice little earner for Panasonic, if anyone is 'stupid' enough to want to have their gadgets last a long time these days.<br /><br />Talk about encouraging waste and re-consumption. The economics of everything is reversed: once it used to be cost-effective to keep the main device going well into the future; now it's all about rebuying it again.<br /><br />AA BATTERIES<br />The great thing with this shaver is it takes standard AA batteries which can be quickly swapped instead of waiting for an internal non-removable battery to charge. This is what attracted me the most. The honest-to-goodness standard AA batteries. Make mine rechargeable please (and not alkaline), and make batteries easily replaceable/swappable.<br /><br />As I mentioned earlier, alkaline is mentioned no less than 3 times on the back of the packaging. I shake my head. And to think that people will be doing exactly what Panasonic suggests and warns against in the manual. It makes me die a little on the inside; it really does. Just multiply that by thousands (millions?) of users of this product and many thousands of batteries sitting in landfill.<br /><br />This is 2013 isn't it?<br />Yet we are still wasting our resources away like crazy.<br /><br />PERFORMANCE<br />With all that said, I am not that impressed with the shaver; it won't shave as close as a blade but it can (in parts) do just that; it will just take far longer than you think and always leave spots. It won't be anywhere near as fast as a blade, but it can (in parts) be effective. Under the chin and neck, it's pretty bad, whether wet or dry and it takes some extensive time to be shaved well.<br /><br />It took me far longer to get a complete shave than a razor, and even then it wasn't quite clean. Initially I thought it was surprisingly good given the lowsih price and limitations of travel and whatever (occasional use) but it's really not very practical to me. On the plus side, it seems to be constructed well and designed pretty well.<br /><br />Cleaning up seems pretty easy too and the manual is mostly illustrated well, so that's good. The parts are labelled clearly. The manual offers instructions in both English and Spanish and is brief and to-the-point and is otherwise clearly understandable.<br /><br />SUMMARY<br />Not the fastest shaver you've ever had.<br />Not the closest shaver you've ever had.<br />In fact, you may be downright disappointed.<br /><br />It's not unexpected for what you pay, though, but if you are used to shaving with a blade, I'd say avoid this product unless you are curious to see what a very low cost shaver can do.<br /><br />Regarding alkaline batteries again...<br />Panasonic, please provide a technical reason why you insist on alkalines so strongly and warn against rechargeables, particularly in light of the fact that alkalines themselves can leak too.<br /><br />I'd love to hear back.to-the-point.<br /><br />Though it is dumb-as-bricks with its alkaline insistence.<br />With all that said...<br /><br />Panasonic, you already own the best AA/AAA Ni-MH low-self-discharge battery technology the world has to offer (Sanyo Eneloop) and it's truly heartbreaking to hear that ugly alkaline word mentioned in 2013.<br /><br />I'm sincerely dying to know why you'd suggest leakage with rechargeables when alkalines are known for exactly that.<br /><br />I hope we can move beyond the world of disposable batteries forever with your help. And that starts in the user guides and packaging.<br /><br />Panasonic, please provide a technical reason why you insist on alkalines so strongly and warn against rechargeables, particularly in light of the fact that alkalines themselves can leak too.<br /><br />I'm waiting to hear from you.<br />Sincerely.

  768. Along with this, I've also owned a few low end rotary electrics, and a mid-tier foil style razor. As you go up in price, you tend to be able to shave more quickly, though the final result is similar. The rotaries I've tried seem to do a slightly better job at the underchin area (the toughest place for electrics), but not by much. The drawback with the ES3831 is that while powerful, there's a lot of vibration. Although all the manuals for electrics will say not to push against your skin, it does help to press a bit get a closer shave. It's tougher to get a feel for how much pressure to apply (to avoid irritating the skin excessively or pressing past the hair) when the razor's shaking so much. A $45 rotary model by Philips is much more sedate in comparison, allowing more precise use. It seems to be power efficient, as the batteries last a very long time - longer than a single charge on the rotary rechargeable I have. The fact that it uses AA batteries makes it great for travel - there's no adapter to bring. I use rechargables, and those provide plenty of juice for most trips. It's a no-frills shaver, but nevertheless built solidly with a nice dense weight to it. Great - for the cost.
